What am I? When derived from a Latin meaning to stretch, I describe the state of an object that is stretched tight. However, when derived from a Latin noun meaning time, I am used when describing the present, future, and perfect in Latin. ANSWER:TENSE BONUS: What am I? When derived from a noun meaning soil, I am the undersurface of a foot. However, when derived from a Latin adjective meaning alone, I share the same meaning as that Latin root. ANSWER:SURELY A GOOD FARMER IS PREPARED WHEN WOLVES APPEAR IN HIS GARDEN? BONUS: Now translate this sentence: Quando sol e terra venit, quam diu lucet, et quando nocti cedit? ANSWER:WHEN DOES THE SUN COME OUT OF THE EARTH, HOW LONG DOES IT SHINE, AND WHEN DOES IT YIELD TO THE NIGHT? 
Translate the following sentence from English to Latin: Read many books, Quintus, and you will see many places. ANSWER:LEGE MULTOS LIBROS, QUINTE, ET MULTOS LOCOS VIDEBIS. BONUS:Translate this sentence from English to Latin: Slaves, do not give the queen wine! ANSWER:NOLITE, SERVI, REGINAE VINUM DARE. BONUS: Now translate this sentence from English to Latin: Lucretius, tell me a song about nature! ANSWER:DIC/NARRA MIHI, LUCRETI, CARMEN DE NATURA! 
Give a Latin antonym of longus. ANSWER:BREVIS BONUS:Give a Latin antonym of vita. ANSWER:MORS BONUS:Give a Latin antonym of sto. ANSWER:SEDEO 
Tense, tempest, contemporary, and temporal are all derived from what Latin noun? ANSWER:TEMPUS BONUS:Terrace, terrier, disinter, and terrestrial are all derived from what Latin noun? ANSWER:TERRA BONUS:Obviate, trivial, voyage, and deviate are all derived from what Latin noun? ANSWER:VIA 
Complete the following analogy. Pater:: Mater as Filius::__________. ANSWER:FILIA BONUS: Complete the following analogy. Filius:: Filiīs as Filia::__________. ANSWER:FILIABUS BONUS:Give another first declension feminine noun that follows the same construction in the ablative and dative plural as fila. ANSWER:DEA, EQUA, MULA 
We’ll never forget the distracted boyfriend meme from 2017. But have you forgotten your derivatives? From what Latin verb, with what meaning, is “distracted” derived? ANSWER:TRAHŌ, DRAG BONUS:The expanding galaxy brain is still present in our consciousness. From what noun, with what meaning, is “galaxy” derived? ANSWER:LĀC, MILK BONUS: The Gandalf “you shall not pass” meme is another memorable specimen. From what noun that means “step”, is “pass” derived? PASSUS ANSWER:NOVICE SEMI 
What English word, derived from ardeo, means “the criminal act of deliberately setting fire to property?” ANSWER:ARSON BONUS:What English word, derived from gaudeo, means “ostentatiously ornamented” or “flashy?” ANSWER:GAUDY BONUS:What English word, derived from facio, means “to challenge the power of” or “resist boldly?” ANSWER:DEFY 
Count from one to five in Latin cardinal numbers. ANSWER:UNUS/A/UM, DUO/AE, TRES/TRIA, QUATTOR, QUINQUE BONUS: Now count from one to five in Latin ordinal numbers. ANSWER:PRIMUS, SECUNDUS, TERTIUS, QUARTUS, QUINTUS, BONUS: Now count from eighteen to twenty in Latin cardinal numbers. ANSWER:DUODEVIGINTI, UNDEVIGINTI, VIGINTI 
Give the idiomatic meaning of Ad Kalendas Graecas. ANSWER:NEVER BONUS:What does the phrase ab ovo usque ad mala mean idiomatically? ANSWER:FROM BEGINNING TO END/FROM SOUP TO NUTS BONUS:What does the phrase de gustibus non est disputandum mean idiomatically? THERE IS NO ACCOUNTING FOR TASTES / ANSWER:EVERYONE TO HIS OWN TASTE 
What do all of the following Latin nouns have in common grammatically? gelu, pecu, genu, and cornu ANSWER:FOURTH DECLENSION NEUTER [PROMPT ON “FOURTH DECLENSION” or “NEUTER”] BONUS:Give a masculine first declension noun. AGRICOLA / AURIGA / ATHLETA / ANSWER:INCOLA / POETA / NAUTA / PIRATA BONUS:Give another. ANSWER:SEE ABOVE 
At what kind of events might a Roman hear all the following words or phrases: Camillus, pronuba, mustaceum, ubi tu Gaius ego Gaia? ANSWER:WEDDINGS BONUS:Which type of Roman wedding, originally practiced only by patricians, required ten witnesses and featured a cake of spelt called mustaceum? ANSWER:CONFARREATIO BONUS:Which other type of Roman wedding required 5 witnesses and featured the fictitious sale of the bride to the groom? ANSWER:COEMPTIO 
Complete the following analogy. Amo :: Amate as Ago::__________. ANSWER:AGITE BONUS:Complete the following analogy. Amo :: Amavit as Fero :: __________. ANSWER:TULIT BONUS:Complete the following analogy. Amo :: Amati Sunt as Fero :: __________. ANSWER:LATI SUNT 
Translate the following sentence from English to Latin: Evil words wound both gods and men. ANSWER:MALA VERBA VULNERANT ET DEOS ET HOMINES. BONUS:Translate this sentence from English to Latin, using the verb transferre and the noun sententia: Either you will translate this sentence, or I will translate it. AUT (TU) HANC SENTENTIAM TRANSFERES, ANSWER:AUT (EGO) (EAM) TRANSFERAM. BONUS: Now translate this sentence from English to Latin: Neither one wolf nor a hundred will frighten me in a garden. ANSWER:NEQUE/NEC UNUS LUPUS NEQUE/NEC CENTUM ME IN HORTO TERREBUNT. 
When recognized by the spotter, perform the following command: Sta uno pede et bis sali. ANSWER:PLAYER STANDS ON ONE FOOT AND JUMPS TWICE. BONUS:When recognized by the spotter, perform the following command: Surgite omnes et cantante partem carminis “Forma Tui” ANSWER:ALL PLAYERS RISE AND SING SOME OF SHAPE OF YOU BY ED SHEERAN BONUS:When recognized by the spotter, perform the following command: Plaudite dum ridetis. ANSWER:MULTIPLE PLAYERS CLAP WHILE SMILING OR LAUGHING

What is the meaning of the Latin word sordidus? ANSWER:DIRTY BONUS:What is the meaning of the Latin word attonitus? ANSWER:SHOCKED / ASTONISHED BONUS:What is the meaning of the Latin word sollicitus? ANSWER:WORRIED 
Of the nouns: aetas, hiems, lac, vinum, and poena, which is being described in the following Latin sentence: Populus hominem nivis potest facere et Saturnaliam potest celebrare. ANSWER:HIEMS BONUS:Which is being described in the following Latin sentence: Liberi hoc debent bibere sed pauci hoc non potest bibere. ANSWER:LAC BONUS:Which is being described in the following Latin sentence: Scelesti homines hoc merent quod mala egerunt. ANSWER:POENA 
Complete the following analogy. Ambulo :: Ambulabo as Sum::__________. ANSWER:ERO BONUS:Sum:: Ero as Possum ::__________. ANSWER:POTERO BONUS:Possum :: Potero as Fio ::__________. ANSWER:FIAM 
What case do all of the following take? misereor, instar, memini, obliviscor. ANSWER:GENTITIVE BONUS:What case do all of the following take? potior, vescor, fungor, utor. ANSWER:ABLATIVE BONUS: What case do all of the following take? noceo, impero, invideo. ANSWER:DATIVE 
Which two words from the following list are derived from the same Latin root: tent, tentacle, detention, pretentious? ANSWER:TENT, PRETENTIOUS BONUS:Which two words from this list are derived from the same Latin root: apparel, appear, parent, compare?
